  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_3869847c-b800-4d90-915f-06396306691b'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText16838829479675977414" style="display:none">Good-bye, Lightning Girl<br /><br />Ever since a walk home on a particularly stormy day, Jessica Mastriani has had an ability like no other. She became known worldwide as Lightning Girl--a psychic who could find the location of anyone, dead or alive. Jess finally had no choice but to embrace her newfound talent, and ended up lending her skills to the U.S. government. <br /><br />But her work for them has taken a terrible toll, and Jess resurfaces months later a shadow of her former self, her powers gone, Lightning Girl no more. Her only hope is starting over in a new place, a big city where nobody knows her.<br /><br />It's only when Rob Wilkins unexpectedly shows up on her doorstep that she's forced to face her past. Rob, all the way from back home, needs her help. But how can Jess, her powers gone, find anyone, let alone the sister of a man she once loved . . . when she can't even find herself? <br /><br /><i>Missing You</i>, the fifth and final book in the 1-800-Where-R-You series</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2435673589637427416">OH. MY. GOD.<br/><br/><b>Five fucking stars.</b><br/><br/>This was <i>so</i> good I'm gonna cry! Scratch that-- I <i>am</i> crying.<br/><br/>Meg Cabot is one of my most favorite authors ever! I don't know what the book world would do without her and her writing, because <i>damn</i> does this woman know how to write a book!<br/>I loved each and every second of it! I LOVED Jess, I loved Rob, I loved Dougie, I loved Ruth, I LOVED Mr. Mastriani, I thought Karen Sue was an alrighty at the end-- I didn't hate her.<br/>OVERALL I loved <i>everything</i>!<br/>I just hated Boobs-As-B</span>
  <span id="freeText2435673589637427416" style="display:none">OH. MY. GOD.<br /><br /><b>Five fucking stars.</b><br /><br />This was <i>so</i> good I'm gonna cry! Scratch that-- I <i>am</i> crying.<br /><br />Meg Cabot is one of my most favorite authors ever! I don't know what the book world would do without her and her writing, because <i>damn</i> does this woman know how to write a book!<br />I loved each and every second of it! I LOVED Jess, I loved Rob, I loved Dougie, I loved Ruth, I LOVED Mr. Mastriani, I thought Karen Sue was an alrighty at the end-- I didn't hate her.<br />OVERALL I loved <i>everything</i>!<br />I just hated Boobs-As-Big-As-My-Head and wanted to crack her skull open, along with Randy Sr. and Jr.<br /><br />But <i>man</i> I'm so sad the series is over! This is probably the 4th time (Yes, Im counting) I have ever laughed so much in my entire life after finishing a book series! (The others being TMI + TID and The Hex Hall series)<br />Meg Cabot is a natural and I love that about her. I love how she portrays the character herself and engages with the reader through text, because I could feel and understand Jess with what she was doing. I absolutely adore Jess, I can't stop saying it.<br /><br />I'm so glad I read this series after finishing The Mediator series which I also adored! :")<br />I really hope Meg writes more books like these-- and I really do hope that Authors can try and make characters as amazing as Jessica!<br />Forget Katniss dudes, this girl is my <b>MY NEW GIRL CRUSH.<br />I LOVE YOU JESS. </b><br /><br /><b>LOVED IT. I HIGHLY HIGHLY HIGHLY RECOMMENDED THIS SERIES.</b></span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17154113544283508181">This is my favourite series by Meg Cabot. There is something endearing about Jess Mastriani, a dedicated flute player with anger management problems and quick fists, and Rob Wilkins, who just happens to be one of the sexiest characters this author has created ( a guy who knows his mind, works hard and above all, waits for the girl ). It's great to see how all the loose ends get tied in this final book, although I am going to miss this series.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12550278706727869814">Before we get into this review, there are some things you should probably know. <br/><br/>I LOVE Jess Mastriani. <br/>I adore Rob Wilkins. <br/>I have loved this series from the first book. <br/>I am soooooooo sad that its over. <br/>I was apparently absent the day in 4th grade where they though you not to start every sentence with "I".<br/><br/><br/>Now that the business has been taking care of, I just adore this series. I can't say enough how much I love a good spunky and snarky heroine, and Jess definitely has that down. She is funny, s</span>
  <span id="freeText12550278706727869814" style="display:none">Before we get into this review, there are some things you should probably know. <br /><br />I LOVE Jess Mastriani. <br />I adore Rob Wilkins. <br />I have loved this series from the first book. <br />I am soooooooo sad that its over. <br />I was apparently absent the day in 4th grade where they though you not to start every sentence with "I".<br /><br /><br />Now that the business has been taking care of, I just adore this series. I can't say enough how much I love a good spunky and snarky heroine, and Jess definitely has that down. She is funny, silly, feisty, and really makes me relate to her. I get hot and flustered with Rob when she does too, because I am soooo right there with her. And if Rob is half as hot in real life as he is in my head, then DAMN. <br /><br />I didn't buy this series at first, I got it from the library, all except for this book, which I was planning on donating to the library- but now I think I'll keep them and just buy them all. Yes that's how much I love them. But as Levar Burton says, "You don't have to take my word for it"<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12550278706727869814" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/21230957?book_show_action=true">Apr 29, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer Wardrip" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer Wardrip" href="/user/show/1125613-jennifer-wardrip">Jennifer Wardrip</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1125613-jennifer-wardrip?shelf=read-by-other-reviewers">read-by-other-reviewers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1125613-jennifer-wardrip?shelf=trt-posted-reviews">trt-posted-reviews</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer21230957" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5358488830163272710">Reviewed by Randstostipher "tallnlankyrn" Nguyen for TeensReadToo.com<br/><br/>After a very long wait, readers will be able to find closure with the last book in one of Meg Cabot's hit series, 1-800-WHERE-R-YOU. Ms. Cabot begins the novel almost two years after the last book. Jessica Mastriana is now at Julliard after the long, tedious days she spent helping the U.S. government find the bad guys during war. Although it did help her country, the things she saw as she was overseas took a toll on her. Instea</span>
  <span id="freeText5358488830163272710" style="display:none">Reviewed by Randstostipher "tallnlankyrn" Nguyen for TeensReadToo.com<br /><br />After a very long wait, readers will be able to find closure with the last book in one of Meg Cabot's hit series, 1-800-WHERE-R-YOU. Ms. Cabot begins the novel almost two years after the last book. Jessica Mastriana is now at Julliard after the long, tedious days she spent helping the U.S. government find the bad guys during war. Although it did help her country, the things she saw as she was overseas took a toll on her. Instead of being able to dream about missing people, now Jess only dreams about the horrible scenes she saw during the war. This ultimately leads to her losing her powers. <br /><br />But now that is all behind her. It's summer and Jess is living with her best friend, Ruth, along with Michael and Skip, and is helping to teach kids how to play a musical instrument. All Jess wants to do is to forget about the past and start over. <br /><br />Unfortunately, her plans are ruined when her ex-boyfriend Rob flies all the way to New York to see her. But it's not to ask her to get back together with her--more like Rob needs Jess to help him find his sister, who just went missing. Before she knows it, all the things that Jess wanted to forget come crashing back. But with her powers supposedly gone, how can she help Rob, the one person she especially wants to forget about? <br /><br />After the long wait, we expected for this series to end with a bang, and Ms. Cabot does not disappoint. MISSING YOU is the perfect ending to the 1-800-WHERE-R-YOU series, tying up all loose ends and resolving all problems, leaving the reader with no unanswered questions. Most characters return in the story, and even a surprise romance begins. Readers will root for Jess until the very end, while falling head-over-heels for Rob all over again. The only sad part is, now the series is completely over! </span>
  <a data-text-id="5358488830163272710" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1097302344" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1097302344" />
    <a title="Nasty Lady MJ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4026143-nasty-lady-mj"><img alt="Nasty Lady MJ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506395877p2/4026143.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1097302344?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nasty Lady MJ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nasty Lady MJ" href="/user/show/4026143-nasty-lady-mj">Nasty Lady MJ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1097302344" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1972444807296820473">I think the rating for this one holds. I actually liked it better than the third and fourth book now, but it is fairly weak still. The characters just feel odd post time jump. And really I feel like Jess should be older than 19 for this story.<br/><br/>Also, it really annoys me how every YA character that Meg has post YA time period is involved with something with kid's-Jess teaches music, Suze is a freaking guidance counselor (which was probably the worst of the lot of the careers), and Mia has that stup</span>
  <span id="freeText1972444807296820473" style="display:none">I think the rating for this one holds. I actually liked it better than the third and fourth book now, but it is fairly weak still. The characters just feel odd post time jump. And really I feel like Jess should be older than 19 for this story.<br /><br />Also, it really annoys me how every YA character that Meg has post YA time period is involved with something with kid's-Jess teaches music, Suze is a freaking guidance counselor (which was probably the worst of the lot of the careers), and Mia has that stupid tutoring center. While the career sort of works for Jess it doesn't work for the other characters and it makes me roll my eyes.<br /><br />Also, the stupid elementary school plot is sort of rehashed in the Boy is Back. <br /><br />Anyway, may have to take a break from my Cabot reread binge and read something else. I pray to God that the Mediator series holds because 1800 Where R U was a bit of a disappointment to say the least. <br /><br />To see full review click <a href="http://howdyyal.wordpress.com/2014/11/07/jessica-you-do-know-google-locate-sort-of-made-you-obsolete-1800-where-r-you-series-by-meg-cabot/" rel="nofollow noopener">here.</a><br /><br />This isn’t a bad book but there is a big disconnect between it and the other four books.<br /><br />To be fair there were a lot of outside factors contributing to the disconnect. The fact that this book was published years after book four. The fact that it was originally intended on being a long series and Cabot had to stuff the end into one book.<br /><br />So, those factors contributed it was a nice send off.<br /><br />Not the best send off though.<br /><br />I really wish the 1800 series would’ve been given two books not one by Harper to finish things off. But beggars can’t be choosers.<br /><br />I think by itself Missing You isn’t that bad. It has a nice well rounded plot (perfectly predictable, but good enough). And the characters aren’t awful.<br /><br />But they aren’t themselves either.<br /><br />It almost seems like during the years in between the publication of Sanctuary and Missing You, Meg sort of lost sense of these characters. And I know, it was probably because of the time jump, but I just didn’t like it.<br /><br />I didn’t like Jess’s mad punching skills being reduced to nothing (seriously, she can’t defend herself at the end, Cabot, for reals?). And Rob was acting just weird.<br /><br />Sorry, the more I reflect on it that scrapbook thing was sort of creepy.<br /><br />It’s not the worst finale in the world, but after binging on the four previous installments it just sort of sticks out.<br /><br />And I’ll admit, when I first read this book I was in awe but now I’m just sort of over it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1972444807296820473" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8488320193257306431">Original review posted <a href='http://boundwithwords.blogspot.com.br/2015/03/that-time-when-i-got-too-lazy-to-write.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>here.</a><br/><br/>3.5<br/><br/>Okay, so for those who don't know 1-800-Where-R-You is a series about Jess, who was a normal girl until she got hit by a lighting and started finding people and this is the last book of the series.<br/><br/>The first thing that put me off on this book was the fact that it had passed so much time since the last one! On the fourth one Jess isn't even finished with high school or is old enough to officially date Rob but them we start this one and years had passed, Jess had went</span>
  <span id="freeText8488320193257306431" style="display:none">Original review posted <a href="http://boundwithwords.blogspot.com.br/2015/03/that-time-when-i-got-too-lazy-to-write.html" rel="nofollow noopener">here.</a><br /><br />3.5<br /><br />Okay, so for those who don't know 1-800-Where-R-You is a series about Jess, who was a normal girl until she got hit by a lighting and started finding people and this is the last book of the series.<br /><br />The first thing that put me off on this book was the fact that it had passed so much time since the last one! On the fourth one Jess isn't even finished with high school or is old enough to officially date Rob but them we start this one and years had passed, Jess had went to the army (!!) and was all messed up and I didn't even knew why she was messed up (I mean, in theory I knew, but I would have liked to read about that time too).<br /><br />Taking that away I had a great time with this book, as I always have with the books on this series (or just Meg Cabot books in general, really). We have a new case and Jess has a lot of things to cover but most important, SHE IS FINALLY OLD ENOUGH TO DATE ROB!!! So yeah, lots of interesting things, super recommended to lovers of this series or of Meg Cabot books.</span>

<div id="review_57908303" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/57908303" />
    <a title="Jessi Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2348498-jessi-rose"><img alt="Jessi Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1436151949p2/2348498.jpg" /></a>

<div id="review_89777994" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/89777994" />
    <a title="Nan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/754607-nan"><img alt="Nan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1277820071p2/754607.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/89777994?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nan" href="/user/show/754607-nan">Nan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/754607-nan?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/754607-nan?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/754607-nan?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/754607-nan?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer89777994" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9081184577939632549">I posted a short review of the first book in this series, and now I'll post a short review of the series as a whole.<br/><br/>I've read nearly everything that Meg Cabot has written. While some parts of this series were familiar to me as a Cabot fan (the tough heroine, ready with a punch, the parents that simply don't understand), this series was a real departure from her norm.<br/><br/>In her blog, Cabot has written that 9/11 never happened in Mia's world (the heroine of the Princess Diaries). 9/11 did happen here-</span>
  <span id="freeText9081184577939632549" style="display:none">I posted a short review of the first book in this series, and now I'll post a short review of the series as a whole.<br /><br />I've read nearly everything that Meg Cabot has written. While some parts of this series were familiar to me as a Cabot fan (the tough heroine, ready with a punch, the parents that simply don't understand), this series was a real departure from her norm.<br /><br />In her blog, Cabot has written that 9/11 never happened in Mia's world (the heroine of the Princess Diaries). 9/11 did happen here--and so did the war in Afghanistan, if not in Iraq. Unlike her other works, Cabot confronts real issues and real life problems in this book--internet predators, porn, post traumatic stress syndrome. Jess' brother has schizophrenia, and this series could be said to be about his recovery as much as Jess'. These real problems make the stakes in Jess' life seem even more powerful.<br /><br />I would highly recommend this book to any Cabot fan that would like to see her stretch beyond what's familiar.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9081184577939632549" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_161221599" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/161221599" />
    <a title="Karen Keyte" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3164510-karen-keyte"><img alt="Karen Keyte" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1263860035p2/3164510.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/161221599?book_show_action=true">Apr 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karen Keyte" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karen Keyte" href="/user/show/3164510-karen-keyte">Karen Keyte</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3164510-karen-keyte?shelf=teen-girls-adventure-mystery">teen-girls-adventure-mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer161221599" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10880930583953469463">Missing You, the fifth and final book in Meg Cabot's 1-800-Where-R-You series, takes place several years after the events of the first four books. Jess, now nineteen, is at the lowest point of her life. Having agreed to use her freaky psychic power for finding people (gained when she was hit by lighting) in the service of the U.S. Government - specifically Dr. Cyrus Krantz and his group of psychic special operatives - Jess has recently returned from the war in Afghanistan exhausted, emotionally </span>
  <span id="freeText10880930583953469463" style="display:none">Missing You, the fifth and final book in Meg Cabot's 1-800-Where-R-You series, takes place several years after the events of the first four books. Jess, now nineteen, is at the lowest point of her life. Having agreed to use her freaky psychic power for finding people (gained when she was hit by lighting) in the service of the U.S. Government - specifically Dr. Cyrus Krantz and his group of psychic special operatives - Jess has recently returned from the war in Afghanistan exhausted, emotionally scarred and devoid of her psychic powers. Despite suffering from post-traumatic stress, Jess is relatively normal for the first time since the fateful lighting strike three years before.<br /><br />Jess isn't sure what she expected when she moved to New York to study music at Juilliard, but she surely expected to be a whole lot happier than she currently is. In fact, she's not only dissatisfied, she's restless, at loose ends and not sure what she wants to do with her life. When she opens her apartment door one evening and finds her ex, Rob Wilkins (the boy Jess was once convinced was the love of her life) standing on her doorstep, Jess isn't even sure if she's happy to see him. As it turns out, Rob isn't in New York for a happy reunion. He needs Jess to try and reawaken her powers so he can find his missing sister.<br /><br />Missing You is a fitting finale for this thoroughly enjoyable series. In keeping with the maturity of the characters, the themes are more adult and somewhat darker and Jess is a little less exuberant and slightly more cerebral (although no one would ever call her subdued). I love that Meg Cabot wrote this book for all of the readers who wanted to know what happened to Jess and Rob. Missing You not only delivers a wholly satisfactory ending to this series, it's a great story all on its own.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10880930583953469463" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13951664636324900808">This book is the final book in the 1-800-where-r-you series, by meg cabot. I think it's definitely the best one. After Jessica Mastriani is hit by lightening, she discovers that she has unique powers to find the location of any body, whether they are dead, or alive. After using her powers to find missing people she can't help but know their whereabouts, she ends up helping the US government, with the war.   <span id="freeText13951664636324900808" style="display:none">This book is the final book in the 1-800-where-r-you series, by meg cabot. I think it's definitely the best one. After Jessica Mastriani is hit by lightening, she discovers that she has unique powers to find the location of any body, whether they are dead, or alive. After using her powers to find missing people she can't help but know their whereabouts, she ends up helping the US government, with the war. Working for them does not work for long, because 6 months later, struck by the horrors of war, Jess's powers disappear, and she returns home, a shadow of her old self. She's attending Juilliard, and sharing an apartment with her best friend and brother, lying to herself about what she really wants, and she hasn't had much contact with her family and friends back home. Then Rob Wilkins shows up, her old boyfriend who she has always loved- and asks for her help. They go on a mission to find Rob's missing sister, and along the way, Jess begins to "repair" herself, and start to understand things she's never understood about Rob before. <br /><br />So it's a very good book. There's some mystery, fantasy, and romance in it, and I really reccomend it!!! (You should read the whole series, but this one is the best of them all)<br />:):):)</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer245852862" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17294574819124804024">Meeeehhh....I can't help but feel like this is sort of a disappointing ending to this series. It's just so removed from the rest of it. I suppose it doesn't help that we've skipped ahead three years. The pacing is off, too. It's like Ms. Cabot just didn't want to continue this series. But I'm thankful she finished it and gave us some sense of closure regarding Jessie, Rob, and the rest. Despite its strange, out-of-place feel in regards to the rest of the series, I still enjoyed it.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Aadila" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16770676-aadila"><img alt="Aadila" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1461939873p2/16770676.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1337061015?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aadila" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aadila" href="/user/show/16770676-aadila">Aadila</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1337061015" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17550226656057574593">Reread the series: 2020<br/><br/>So, my faith in Meg Cabot has been restored until shaken otherwise.<br/><br/>Overall I quite enjoyed the series. Jess is a fun character to follow - at times I wished she would be less flippant and that we could get to see a more emotional side to her - but I feel like in this book which reads as an epilogue to the series, we finally got to see that. <br/><br/>I loved that the romance was a secondary thread in the story and was only really brought to the forefront in this last book. Rob is by</span>
  <span id="freeText17550226656057574593" style="display:none">Reread the series: 2020<br /><br />So, my faith in Meg Cabot has been restored until shaken otherwise.<br /><br />Overall I quite enjoyed the series. Jess is a fun character to follow - at times I wished she would be less flippant and that we could get to see a more emotional side to her - but I feel like in this book which reads as an epilogue to the series, we finally got to see that. <br /><br />I loved that the romance was a secondary thread in the story and was only really brought to the forefront in this last book. Rob is by far one of my favourite Meg Cabot male leads. <br /><br />I wouldn't say I was completely invested in the side characters but at the same time I didn't dislike them. In the end it was nice knowing where everyone was in their lives and seeing how they'd all matured and grown. Although I do wish Jess's relationship with her Mum was fleshed out a bit more since they clearly had major communication issues.<br /><br />My biggest gripe is I wish that in earlier books certain events hadn't been so implausible. Biker gangs blowing up a FBI/military helicopter and busting onto a military base to save Jess or biker gangs going head to head with an armed and dangerous cult...firstly this would never happen and secondly definitely not without consequence. But in Jess's world things always seem to work out alright in the end if you were one of the good guys.<br /><br />(Speaking of implausible - I don't know how I felt about Jess going to Afghanistan. To me it didn't really fit in to the story or the character. I much prefer the route which the television series took where Jess trained to become an actual FBI agent and had a partner, etc.)<br /><br />To sum up, a fun read as long as you ignore implausible events and the occasional offensive line (like both Jess and Rob offensively mentioning Ruth's weight in Book 1- why?? Just why? I just remembered this and now I feel weird about saying Rob is one of my fav male leads. Sigh).</span>
  <a data-text-id="17550226656057574593" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <span class="greyText">Recommended to FoodxHugs by: </span>
      no one, just me

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32614001-foodxhugs?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32614001-foodxhugs?shelf=childhood-nostalgia">childhood-nostalgia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32614001-foodxhugs?shelf=book-series">book-series</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1704342078" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6191986558325962502">Again, the mystery element was kind of --pardon the pun-- missing. The plot is similar to the last book (and grown-up instalment) in the Mediator series Remembrance. It seems Meg Cabot has a thing for pedo/porn rings. There are other types of crimes, you know...<br/><br/>Her villains are unmemorable and nearly always males in her paranormal mysteries. <br/><br/>Our heroine, "Lightning Girl", Jess Mastriani is 19 years old and no longer working for the FBI. After coming back home broken from war service in Afghanist</span>
  <span id="freeText6191986558325962502" style="display:none">Again, the mystery element was kind of --pardon the pun-- missing. The plot is similar to the last book (and grown-up instalment) in the Mediator series Remembrance. It seems Meg Cabot has a thing for pedo/porn rings. There are other types of crimes, you know...<br /><br />Her villains are unmemorable and nearly always males in her paranormal mysteries. <br /><br />Our heroine, "Lightning Girl", Jess Mastriani is 19 years old and no longer working for the FBI. After coming back home broken from war service in Afghanistan, she just wants to be normal and imagines herself settling down in the future. Unfortunately, her ex Rob Wilkins travels from Indiana to New York, where she is studying at music school Juilliard, and disrupts her plans because his sister is missing.<br /><br />Jess recovers the use of her latent powers and helps him find the brattish girl. Side characters from the previous four books in the series make a tiny appearance like Jess's brothers, her parents and her best friend Ruth. <br /><br />The romance element is strained and there isn't much chemistry between Jess and Rob. She seemed wingy, brittle and closed off while he didn't seem like the bad boy he was made out to be in earlier books, especially after we found out what he was convicted of. <br /><br />Everyone had the same speech patterns and phrases so dialogue isn't Cabot's strong point. Neither is the text description heavy, which makes it a fast read, if not exactly evocative in place and tone.<br /><br />This is a better resolution than Remembrance, so it wasn't all bad. But Meg Cabot definitely needs to be adventurous in her plots because they're all starting to resemble each other.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6191986558325962502" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <a title="Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo" href="/user/show/1011913-jo">Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1011913-jo?shelf=2009">2009</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1011913-jo?shelf=fantasy-and-paranormal">fantasy-and-paranormal</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer71549670" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7898837758645375685">I have very mixed feeling about this finale. I always like happy endings, especially neat and tidy happy endings. Especially when the neat and tidy happy endings can be believable. But I'm not sure I thought this one was believable. I guess it wasn't unbelievable, but.... Couldn't the FBI still be all annoying and persistent? Maybe not Dr. Krantz, but what about an even-higher-up? I'm not thrilled with the cover art, but I hate all the new cover art people are coming up with. And I'm not thrille</span>
  <span id="freeText7898837758645375685" style="display:none">I have very mixed feeling about this finale. I always like happy endings, especially neat and tidy happy endings. Especially when the neat and tidy happy endings can be believable. But I'm not sure I thought this one was believable. I guess it wasn't unbelievable, but.... Couldn't the FBI still be all annoying and persistent? Maybe not Dr. Krantz, but what about an even-higher-up? I'm not thrilled with the cover art, but I hate all the new cover art people are coming up with. And I'm not thrilled with the non-marital "relations," but I am aware that not everyone views these things the same way I do. And at least they were engaged. Which is better than the nothing one so often hears about. But, despite these nit-picky whats-its of mine and my inability to decide how believable I find the neat and tidy package things got all wrapped up in, I still enjoyed reading the book (three hours), and may one day decide to reread the series, for nostalgia's sake.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16308012093511704422"><b> Source: I own an ebook copy of this book. </b><br/>Cost: Free<br/><br/><b> Title: </b> Missing You<br/><b> Series: </b> 1800-WHERE-R-U #5<br/><b> Author: </b> Meg Cabot<br/><b> Overall Rating: </b> 4 stars<br/><br/>I really liked this conclusion to the series. <br/><br/>It takes place roughly two/three years after the conclusion of the last and Jess has been through a lot after battling the war in Afghanistan and the war on terror, she's a mess.   <span id="freeText16308012093511704422" style="display:none"><b> Source: I own an ebook copy of this book. </b><br />Cost: Free<br /><br /><b> Title: </b> Missing You<br /><b> Series: </b> 1800-WHERE-R-U #5<br /><b> Author: </b> Meg Cabot<br /><b> Overall Rating: </b> 4 stars<br /><br />I really liked this conclusion to the series. <br /><br />It takes place roughly two/three years after the conclusion of the last and Jess has been through a lot after battling the war in Afghanistan and the war on terror, she's a mess. And it isn't helping that Rob has just shown up at her house asking for her to help find his little sister. <br /><br />There was a lot of character development in this one, the Lightning Girl wasn't so angry anymore. She truly seemed mature enough to deal with her problems and I loved Rob. I've always loved Rob, but he honestly was so nice in this one. We also finally found out what his probation was for, hilarious. No wonder he didn't want to tell Jess.<br /><br />I loved this series and I'm sad that it's over.</span>

  <span id="freeText8439369860208165077" style="display:none">I thought this book was really funny. I love Meg Cabot as an author, she is my favorite. The narrative is spoken like a person is actually talking to you and so it is very relaxed. The plot was really intersting. I think I accidentally read the last book of the series but I wasn't confused when I read it so I don't think it matters. <br />The book is about a girl who was hit by lightning and then has some kind of psychic power that enables her to find people. But she loses her power after she spent a year and a half in Afghanistan helping the marines. She came back with Post-Tramatic-Stress Disorder which had caused her to lose her powers. That's where the story starts, only a year later. She describes how she gets her powers back by helping her friend, Rob, find his sister. Rob was her ex-boyfriend. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6478198731504369976">This book seemed rushed, and some of the things that happened were a little hard to swallow. I did enjoy seeing Rob finally confess his feelings for Jess. I would have preferred a book about the work she did for the government during the war, but that was completely glossed over. The conspiracy that she uncovers was resolved a little too easily to be believable. </span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5504205482938162990">This is my favorite of the 1-800-Where-R-you series. <br/><br/>I was kinda skeptical when I started this book because everything was different. I mean, Jess had her whole non-violence thing going on, they were in New York, Jess lost her powers, and so much more. So yeah, I was a little reluctant.   <span id="freeText5504205482938162990" style="display:none">This is my favorite of the 1-800-Where-R-you series. <br /><br />I was kinda skeptical when I started this book because everything was different. I mean, Jess had her whole non-violence thing going on, they were in New York, Jess lost her powers, and so much more. So yeah, I was a little reluctant. But, from the moment Rob was back, I was the happiest person ever. I swear, how does Meg Cabot have the ability to write the best male characters ever? Rob was soooo sweet in this book! I was literally in a puddle on the floor when I finished this book. I absolutely loved Rob!! &lt;3<br /><br />As usual, the writing was hilarious. I expected nothing less, since every single one of Meg Cabot's books are the funniest things ever. I loved how witty Jess was and how she's literally one of the best main characters ever. <br /><br />Her mom was a little annoying at times, but I liked the end when she welcomed Rob into the family. And her dad was literally the BEST character ever!! He was sooo funny!! <br /><br />But, most of all, I loved this whole series because Meg Cabot somehow managed to put in just enough personal details without making the plot and story drag. Every book of hers gets straight to the point and she never fails to keep me hooked. Especially since her books are never too long and always leave me wanting more. <br /><br />I would love to have another book with Jes and Rob like she did with Princess Diaries and the Mediator. I would definitely read it!! And it's so sad that this series is so hard to find in any library!! It's one of my favs by her. <br /><br />Anyways, this series is one of the best. I loved the main character, and basically every character, the plot, and just everything about this book!!! It's sooooo awesome!!! &lt;3 &lt;3</span>

  <span id="freeText15411972456885226307" style="display:none">I Have thoroughly enjoyed all of these books so much! It Meg Cabot had me hooked, from the first chapter! I enjoyed the story. I enjoyed the characters. I enjoyed everything! I loved how this book kept continuing to amaze. even though I probably should have seen half the plot twists coming. Also I loved how, I wasn't bored, with any of these books. so often with series, I find myself, losing interest as the books go on, because it seems the second, book is never as good as the first, in this case however I feel they all were wrote wonderfully, and I am so glad I took the time to read these books!<br />Spoilers Ahead******<br /><br /><br />Okay so wow! Let's see if I can do this! At first I was so happy that 3 years took place from book 4 to this last book, and in I still am actually pretty happy about it, but I got to say some of the stuff was pretty annoying. But I fully understand why it had to happen. I like how she made Jess grow as a character, I do feel like that needed to happen, and I'm glad she got time to do that! So while reading the first couple of chapters this is what was going through my mind 1 does she have her licence, 2 what happened to Rob 3 she kept Chigger right... I'm gonna be honest I would have been really mad if something happened to Chigger (the dog) He had my heart from the first time we saw him! I mean come on he is so adorable! I wish he was in it more, he would have made an awesome, finding buddy! SO I'm glad he was around. One thing I was sad about was that we never got to see, people from the first books, like Sean, I kind of miss him, and The two agents, Even though I am so guilty of liking Dr Krantz better... I didn't think I would, But lets face it, that guy is awesome! <br />Oh and can we talk about how awesome Jess's dad is! That scene where their talking about her getting her power back, and the tapes, and Rob and pretty much everything, That melted my heart! That was an awesome Father daughter scene! I'm really glad she wrote this book the way she did. Oh and I'm so glad we finally found out what Rob did to get on probation!!!! Trespassing!!!! Wow! Oh and I really love that Mike and Ruth got together, that's cute! So anyway, I really loved this series, am glad I read it, and would definitely recommend</span>

  <span id="freeText9924888983907780789" style="display:none">This book was about a girl named Jessica Mastriani who got hit by lightening when she was a few years younger, and she became known as Lightening Girl, because in her sleep she was able to contact where missing people were. She helped the FBI find criminals and she helped the NAVY find bad guys like Osama Bin Laden, and guys like that.<br />Jess lives in a one bedroom apartment with her best friend since grade school, Ruth. Unfortunately, Ruth's twin brother Skip, and her brother Mike, which isn't good for Jess because Mike and Ruth sleep together.<br />Jessica's ex-boyfriend Robert Wilkins, who was caught kissing another blond-haired-babe who Jess called two different names: 1) Miss-Thanks-For-Fixing-My-Carburetor, and 2) Miss-Breasts-Bigger-Than-My-Head." comes to New York from Indiana to find Jessica to ask her to help him find his sister, Hannah, who he never knew existed. She came to live with him claiming that her mother was a druggie, and that she wanted him to become her legal guardian until she was 18 (she was 15 in the book), turns out that she was staying with a 27 year old guy, named Randy Whitehead Junior, who would have sex with young girls and tape it and when he would dump them off (which he told Hannah he wouldn't do with her because he loved her), and sell the porn tapes internationally.<br />She got him arrested by talking to his father, him and his girlfriend, Kristen in his father's office, where her other brother Douglas and his girlfriend Tasha met them with the police.<br />In the end Rob gives Jess the ring that he would have given her if she didn't run off and let him explain why the blond was kissing him. And if her mother (who didn't approve of him because he was older than Jess), saw that he was doing better because he had his own place and his uncle sold him his garage. Then when he comes to get the ring back from her because he thinks that she won't marry him, she asks him to marry her.<br /><br />This book was okay, I mean I thought there was going to be much more action, but I was wrong. I liked how her ex came back into her life and kind of screwed it up afterwards but it was cool to find out that they got back together and he changed just for her.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer117283307" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16386103468112403348">In MISSING YOU, several years have passed since the end of SANCTUARY. Jess is now 19, has helped fight a war and has returned without her "Lightning Girl" powers and with a case of PTSD. She is living in New York with Ruth, Ruth's twin brother Skip, and Jess's brother Mike and spending her days miserable at Julliard. She and her maybe-boyfriend Rob are long broken-up so, when he shows up at her door wanting help locating his missing half-sister, Jess doesn't quite know what to do.<br/><br/>Meg Cabot had a</span>
  <span id="freeText16386103468112403348" style="display:none">In MISSING YOU, several years have passed since the end of SANCTUARY. Jess is now 19, has helped fight a war and has returned without her "Lightning Girl" powers and with a case of PTSD. She is living in New York with Ruth, Ruth's twin brother Skip, and Jess's brother Mike and spending her days miserable at Julliard. She and her maybe-boyfriend Rob are long broken-up so, when he shows up at her door wanting help locating his missing half-sister, Jess doesn't quite know what to do.<br /><br />Meg Cabot had a huge task filling in the gaps while still moving the story toward a solid conclusion in a relative short amount of pages. I think, having read the entire series one after another, the jump in time was more jarring than it would've been to someone reading the books as they were initially published. The 'A' plot of the book is definitely the relationship (or lack-of) between Rob and Jess with the 'B' plot of Rob's missing sister tossed in there as an excuse to throw Jess and Rob together. While I definitely enjoyed the story and the closure it provided there were a few things that niggled at me throughout. First off, the whole 'everybody ends up in New York' thing felt contrived. Secondly, Rob may've achieved *too much* over the course of just a few years. I never felt throughout the series that Rob needed to throw money around in order to be good enough for Jess--he was good enough already. Also, I question the logic of breaking into homes to steal evidence as it would surely be inadmissible in court.<br /><br />I did think the references to the Lifetime TV series based on the books were cute. Cabot did the same in the Princess Diaries books referencing the movies Disney made. I did enjoy how things were settled between Rob and Jess even if it did seem a bit quick (had there been more books in the series, I'm sure it would've been a more natural progression of events). <br /><br />All in all, it was a good ending to the series that wrapped up the larger loose ends.<br /><br />A note about the Kindle edition: A-OK. Didn't see a single formatting issue. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16386103468112403348" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

      if (form) {

<span id="freeTextContainer540194718692270422">Librarian note: AKA <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/167932.Jenny_Carroll' title='Jenny Carroll' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jenny Carroll</a> (1-800-Where-R-You series), AKA <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/71187.Patricia_Cabot' title='Patricia Cabot' rel='nofollow noopener'>Patricia Cabot</a> (historical romance novels).<br/><br/>Meg Cabot was born on February 1, 1967, during the Chinese astrological year of the Fire Horse, a notoriously unlucky sign. Fortunately she grew up in Bloomington, Indiana, where few people were aware of the stigma of being a fire horse -- at least until Meg became a teenager, when she flun</span>
  <span id="freeText540194718692270422" style="display:none">Librarian note: AKA <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/167932.Jenny_Carroll" title="Jenny Carroll" rel="nofollow noopener">Jenny Carroll</a> (1-800-Where-R-You series), AKA <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/71187.Patricia_Cabot" title="Patricia Cabot" rel="nofollow noopener">Patricia Cabot</a> (historical romance novels).<br /><br />Meg Cabot was born on February 1, 1967, during the Chinese astrological year of the Fire Horse, a notoriously unlucky sign. Fortunately she grew up in Bloomington, Indiana, where few people were aware of the stigma of being a fire horse -- at least until Meg became a teenager, when she flunked freshman Algebra twice, then decided to cut her own bangs. After six years as an undergrad at Indiana University, Meg moved to New York City (in the middle of a sanitation worker strike) to pursue a career as an illustrator, at which she failed miserably, forcing her to turn to her favorite hobby--writing novels--for emotional succor. She worked various jobs to pay the rent, including a decade-long stint as the assistant manager of a 700 bed freshmen dormitory at NYU, a position she still occasionally misses. <br /><br />She is now the author of nearly fifty books for both adults and teens, selling fifteen million copies worldwide, many of which have been #1 New York Times bestsellers, most notably The Princess Diaries series, which is currently being published in over 38 countries, and was made into two hit movies by Disney. In addition, Meg wrote the Mediator and 1-800-Where-R-You? series (on which the television series, Missing, was based), two All-American Girl books, Teen Idol, Avalon High, How to Be Popular, Pants on Fire, Jinx, a series of novels written entirely in email format (Boy Next Door, Boy Meets Girl, and Every Boy's Got One), a mystery series (Size 12 Is Not Fat/ Size 14 Is Not Fat Either/Big Boned), and a chick-lit series called Queen of Babble. <br /><br />Meg is now writing a new children's series called Allie Finkle's Rules for Girls. Her new paranormal series, Abandon, debuts in Summer of 2011. <br /><br />Meg currently divides her time between Key West, Indiana, and New York City with a primary cat (one-eyed Henrietta), various back-up cats, and her husband, who doesn't know he married a fire horse. Please don't tell him. <br /><br /><br /><b>Series:</b><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/45023-airhead" rel="nofollow noopener">Airhead</a><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/43768-the-princess-diaries" rel="nofollow noopener">The Princess Diaries</a><br />* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/41667-mediator" rel="nofollow noopener">Mediator</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="540194718692270422" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
